<Name>Cindy Blankenship< /Name><time>1551503322280<//time>< Rate>
1<//Rate>
< Review>
Our Oliver was a happy 17-year-old kitty with chronic kidney disease (CKD), until we moved back up the mountain and he became too sick to handle the ride down to his former vet. So we took our sweet, loving kitty to Dr. Kim. I liked her high stars and most reviews on G.
I wanted Oliver tested as it'd been a year. Dr. Kim wanted to do a physical exam first before discussing tested options, which made sense as she had never seen Oliver before. We wrongly assumed that when she looked inside his mouth that she would, well look. After Oliver quit eating a few days later, and all the tricks we knew and more didn't work (including pureeing his food), we suspected mouth ulcers (common with CKD cats). I called Dr. Kim's office, and Amanda, a vet tech, told me Dr. Kim would NOT have looked for ulceration in Oliver's mouth. My partner, Bob, told me it seemed she did just a cursory mouth check. I told Amanda that I understood she wasn't going to do a dental check (due to risks of general anesthesia at 17), but since Dr. Kim being a vet, could open his mouth and had looked inside, did she see any ulcers, did she look for ulcers. "No, she did not look for ulcers," I was curtly told. She hadn't looked and wouldn't.  After all, around 80 percent of elderly cats have chronic kidney failure, many developing painful mouth ulcers.

When Dr. Kim examined Oliver, she felt his kidneys and said they were small, maybe 25% function left so testing not necessary at this point - he is in kitty hospice. This at the time made sense due to his age and had entered final stage (4) of CKD last year, but hospice is about comfort and not to look for a painful, common complication of CDK is not right. Yes, it's possible the ulceration happened after he saw the vet, but considering his behaviors, she couldn't take another look, especially since her assistant told me Dr. Kim wouldn't have looked for ulcers the first time - even though he was CKD??? I just wanted him not to suffer (from complications) and die peacefully at home. Or if he did have quality of time with right treatment to be told this based on more than 25% kidney function and small kidneys because many kitties live well with only 10%. I guess I trusted her advice was based on more than that and I didn't question. I am thankful that we were able to care for my loyal companion well enough he enjoyed life through years of CKD. It breaks my heart that we didn't take him down the mountain to his former vet and that because of this he probably died with pain. He passed in my arms, and afterwards I examined his mouth. His gum was puffy and yellow with blood on one side. I told her at the exam he moved his food to the other side. She talked more than listened. And we didn't learn anything new.

I get Dr. Kim wasn't going to have a dental exam done due to age (general anesthesia - he had one down the hill a year ago), but I don't get she couldn't look for ulcers and her tech refused to even bring this up to the vet - just a curt "NO, Dr. Kim doesn't look for ulcers in the mouth." And such a common thing with a common disease in older cats.

I cry everyday. Oliver was the most loyal cat, you would have thought him a dog. A long-haired, beautiful tabby - with Maine Coon. Very sweet. Never reacted poorly at a vet like he did here when the shot hurt him and he clawed his "daddy." I miss him so much, but what bothers me the most is that he was in pain and he didn't need to be. And he didn't need to starve. With future cats, we will drive down the mountain.

Not to mention, because Dr. Kim didn't inform us the B12 shot offered (not needed) would hurt, Oliver dug his claws into Bob, and Dr. Kim didn't offer a sink to cleanse it - nothing.<//Review>

< review>
This place is great! My son played nonstop from 9:30 am to 2 pm. The play structure is amazing, there are so many things for the kids to do: slides, air pressure guns that shoot foam balls, a trampoline with a foam block pit attached, stairs to climb, bridges to traverse, things to climb over and under, places to hide out. They have spaces for younger kids to safely play, a cafe for lunch or snacks and a coffee spot. There is plenty of places to sit around the play areas (they aren't super comfortable but better then nothing and a lot more spots than what I've seen at other indoor playgrounds).
The prices are reasonable also. It depends on your kiddos age and there is no time limit; however, if you leave and come back they will charge a $2 re-entry fee per child...parents are free!<//review>

<review>This place is great for kids! There are 3 separate areas for the kids to play in, helping to keep little ones safe, while still giving the under 4 year olds somewhere fun to play as well. The Lego area is the most popular with my 3 boys, ages 9 and 3. There are a good selection of arcade games, with a good chance to win tickets so the kids can get a few prizes fairly easily.
This whole place is spotless. They really care about cleanliness and it shows. I appreciate the booties at the bathrooms so I don't have to walk in with my socks on.
The coffee shop inside is amazing, with very friendly and helpful baristas. They are always up for creating something new, though everything I've ordered has been great.
I have only had a pretzel from the full snack bar so far, but I thought it was cooked very well. No complaints there.
The staff is very knowledgeable and helpful as well. They are constantly working hard to keep this whole place clean, especially Maddie! She goes above and beyond.
I also like the cost. I don't have to pay by the hour. I can purchase a pass, let the kids play all day, leave for lunch, re-enter for I think $2 each,  then let them play the rest of the day. Way cheaper than any other play place like this!
We will definitely keep coming back.
Thank you!<//review><Pics>None</Pics><user_name>Angela Cline< /user_name>< UserId.>

<review>For the record, I've been eating at various Round Table Pizza restaurants since I was a young. It's my favorite local area pizza chain.
And this particular shop is one that I used to frequent back in the nineties when I had friends that worked there. So I have a pretty good idea of what to expect.
That being said, I really only have one complaint...
If you can't cook the pizza properly (make sure the dough is fully cooked) then maybe Monday Appreciation day should no longer exist.
I get that it's a promotion that fills the joint and that customers, like my wife, really appreciate because of the savings; but I've started to ignore the savings and save my stomach.
Last night was the first time in a while that we've been to this restaurant.
(Del's pizza up the street makes a great Garlic pizza and it's fully cooked, but expensive).
I won't be back again on a Monday as the problem still exists.
The Pizzas are fine on other days. But Mondays are a no go.<//review>< Pictures>

Never hang up if contacting by phone and if by email always make a copy.  Make sure you have them repeat their name several times during the conversation so that there is no doubt who it is and reference the phone conversation with the date and time several times as well.
Since I have every piece of paper including the original contract and every fill since then there is no doubt to what Im stating.
Companies have learned through the tough times of this economic disaster that there are NO consequences for any illegal actions so be prepared for everything including strong-arming and phone harassment.  WINDMILL is a leader in this scam.
